Okay, so I have this physics problem here about sound diffraction from a slit. Let me try to figure it out step by step. The question is asking at what frequency the sound will first disappear at a 45-degree angle from the normal to the speaker face. The options are A. 500 Hz, B. 1,750 Hz, C. 2,750 Hz, D. 3,500 Hz. 

First, I remember that when sound waves pass through a slit, they can diffract, similar to light diffraction. The phenomenon is called single-slit diffraction. The condition for constructive and destructive interference is given by the Fraunhofer diffraction formula, which is:

\[
d \sin \theta = m \lambda
\]

where \(d\) is the width of the slit, \(\theta\) is the angle of diffraction, \(m\) is the order of interference (an integer, 0, 1, 2, ...), \(\lambda\) is the wavelength of the sound wave.

But wait, the question is about the sound disappearing, which means destructive interference. So, the first destructive interference occurs when \(m = 1\). That makes sense because the first minimum happens at \(m = 1\).

Given that the angle is 45 degrees, so \(\theta = 45^\circ\). The width of the slit is 0.14 meters. The speed of sound is given as 350 m/s. We need to find the frequency at which this destructive interference occurs.

Let me write down the known values:

- \(d = 0.14\) m,
- \(\theta = 45^\circ\),
- \(m = 1\),
- \(v = 350\) m/s,
- \(f\) is what we need to find,
- \(\lambda = v / f\).

So, substituting \(\lambda\) into the equation:

\[
d \sin \theta = m \lambda
\]
\[
d \sin \theta = m \frac{v}{f}
\]

We can solve for \(f\):

\[
f = \frac{m v}{d \sin \theta}
\]

Plugging in the numbers:

\[
f = \frac{1 \times 350}{0.14 \times \sin 45^\circ}
\]

I need to compute the sine of 45 degrees. I remember that \(\sin 45^\circ = \sqrt{2}/2 \approx 0.7071\).

So, substituting that in:

\[
f = \frac{350}{0.14 \times 0.7071}
\]

First, compute the denominator:

\(0.14 \times 0.7071 = 0.098999\). Let me check that:

\(0.14 \times 0.7071 = 0.14 \times 0.7 + 0.14 \times 0.0071\).

Wait, 0.14 * 0.7 is 0.098, and 0.14 * 0.0071 is approximately 0.000994. So adding those together, it's approximately 0.098994, which is roughly 0.099.

So, the denominator is approximately 0.099.

Therefore, \(f = 350 / 0.099\).

For a single slit, the diffraction pattern has a central bright spot and then alternating dark and bright bands. The first minimum, where the sound disappears, depends on the size of the slit and the angle at which it's observed.

- λ is the wavelength of the sound
- w is the width of the slit

First, let me recall what I know about diffraction. When a sound wave diffracts around an object, like a slit, it can create a pattern called a diffraction pattern. This pattern has a central bright spot and then alternating dark and bright regions. The first minimum, where the sound disappears for the first time, is called the first-order diffraction minimum.

I think this is a single-slit diffraction problem. The formula for the minima in single-slit diffraction is given by:

$$
d \sin \theta = m \lambda
$$

Where:
- \( d \) is the slit width,
- \( \theta \) is the angle from the normal,
- \( m \) is the order of the minimum (1 for the first minimum),
- \( \lambda \) is the wavelength of the sound.

$$
\lambda = \frac{v}{f}
$$

So, rearranging that, the frequency is:

$$
f = \frac{v}{\lambda}
$$

Okay, so I have this physics problem here about sound diffraction. It says that sound waves are moving at 350 m/s and are diffracting out of a speaker enclosure through a long rectangular slit that's 0.14 m across. The question is asking at about what frequency will the sound first disappear at an angle of 45 degrees from the normal to the speaker face. The options are A. 500 Hz, B. 1,750 Hz, C. 2,750 Hz, and D. 3,500 Hz. It mentions that the correct answer is B. 1,750 Hz, but I need to figure out why.

First, let me recall what I know about sound diffraction. There are different types of diffraction, like single-slit, double-slit, etc. Since the question mentions a long rectangular slit, I think single-slit diffraction is what we're dealing with here.

Single-slit diffraction occurs when sound waves pass through a narrow opening, creating a diffraction pattern on a screen. The pattern consists of a central bright band and then alternating dark and bright bands. The condition for destructive interference, which leads to the dark bands, is given by the single-slit diffraction formula:

$$
d \sin \theta = m \lambda
$$

Where:
- \( d \) is the slit width,
- \( \theta \) is the angle from the normal,
- \( m \) is the order of the minima (m = 1, 2, 3, ...),
- \( \lambda \) is the wavelength of the sound.

The question is asking about the first disappearance, which corresponds to the first minimum, so \( m = 1 \).

Given:
- The speed of sound, \( v = 350 \) m/s,
- The slit width, \( d = 0.14 \) m,
- The angle, \( \theta = 45^\circ \).

First, I need to find the wavelength \( \lambda \) of the sound. Since the speed \( v \) is given, I can use the formula for the speed of sound in air:

$$
v = \lambda f
$$

Where \( f \) is the frequency. So, \( \lambda = \frac{v}{f} \). But wait, I don't know the frequency yet. Hmm, maybe I can rearrange that formula to solve for frequency:

$$
f = \frac{v}{\lambda}
$$

But I don't know \( \lambda \) yet. Alternatively, I can use the diffraction formula to solve for \( \lambda \) since I know \( d \) and \( \theta \), and then use that to find \( f \).

Starting with the diffraction formula:

$$
d \sin \theta = m \lambda
$$

Plugging in the known values:

$$
0.14 \sin 45^\circ = 1 \lambda
$$

I can compute \( \sin 45^\circ \). I remember that \( \sin 45^\circ = \frac{\sqrt{2}}{2} \approx 0.7071 \).

So,

$$
0.14 \times 0.7071 = \lambda
$$

Calculating that:

$$
0.14 \times 0.7071 \approx 0.09899 \text{ m}
$$

So, \( \lambda \approx 0.099 \) m.

Now, since \( \lambda = \frac{v}{f} \), rearranging to find \( f \):

$$
f = \frac{v}{\lambda}
$$

Plugging in the values:

$$
f = \frac{350 \text{ m/s}}{0.099 \text{ m}}
$$

Calculating that:

$$
f \approx \frac{350}{0.099} \approx 3545.555 \text{ Hz}
$$

Alright, so I have this physics problem here about sound diffraction. It says that sound waves are moving at 350 m/s and they're diffracting out of a speaker enclosure with a long rectangular slit that's 0.14 meters across. The question is asking at about what frequency will the sound first disappear at an angle of 45 degrees from the normal to the speaker face. The options are A. 500 Hz, B. 1,750 Hz, C. 2,750 Hz, D. 3,500 Hz. The correct answer is supposed to be B, 1,750 Hz, but let me try to figure out why.

First, I remember that when sound waves diffract around an obstacle, they can constructively and destructively interfere with themselves, causing a phenomenon called diffraction. The slit width plays a role in determining the frequency at which constructive or destructive interference occurs.

The problem mentions a long rectangular slit, so I think the diffraction pattern we'll be dealing with is a single-slit diffraction pattern. For a single slit, the condition for destructive interference (which would cause the sound to disappear) is given by the formula:

$$
d \sin \theta = m \lambda
$$

Where:
- \( d \) is the slit width,
- \( \theta \) is the angle from the normal,
- \( m \) is the order of the maxima or minima (for destructive interference, \( m \) is an integer, usually starting from 1),
- \( \lambda \) is the wavelength of the sound.

Given:
- The angle \( \theta \) is 45 degrees,
- The slit width \( d \) is 0.14 m,
- The speed of sound \( v \) is 350 m/s,
- We need to find the frequency \( f \).

First, let's find the wavelength \( \lambda \) using the speed of sound formula:

$$
\lambda = \frac{v}{f}
$$

But since we don't know \( f \) yet, maybe we can express \( f \) in terms of \( \lambda \).

From the diffraction formula:

$$
d \sin \theta = m \lambda
$$

We can solve for \( \lambda \):

$$
\lambda = \frac{d \sin \theta}{m}
$$

Then, substitute \( \lambda \) back into the speed of sound formula:

$$
\frac{v}{f} = \frac{d \sin \theta}{m}
$$

So,

$$
f = \frac{v}{d \sin \theta / m} = \frac{v m}{d \sin \theta}
$$

Alright, so \( f \) is proportional to \( m \). That means higher orders \( m \) will correspond to higher frequencies.

Given \( \theta = 45^\circ \), let's compute \( \sin 45^\circ \). I remember that \( \sin 45^\circ = \frac{\sqrt{2}}{2} \approx 0.7071 \).

So, plugging in the numbers:

\( v = 350 \) m/s,

\( d = 0.14 \) m,

\( \sin \theta \approx 0.7071 \),

Let me compute \( f \) for \( m = 1 \):

$$
f = \frac{350 \times 1}{0.14 \times 0.7071}
$$

0.14 * 0.7071 ≈ 0.14 * 0.7071.

Let me calculate that:

So total ≈ 0.098 + 0.000994 ≈ 0.098994 m.

So denominator ≈ 0.098994 m.

Then, numerator is 350.

So,

f ≈ 350 / 0.098994 ≈ ?

350 / 0.098994.

Alright, so I have this physics problem here about sound diffraction. The question is about a sound wave moving at 350 m/s diffracting out of a speaker enclosure with a long rectangular slit that's 0.14 m across. The problem is asking at what frequency the sound will first disappear at a 45-degree angle from the normal to the speaker face. The options given are A. 500 Hz, B. 1,750 Hz, C. 2,750 Hz, and D. 3,500 Hz. The correct answer is supposed to be B, 1,750 Hz, but I need to figure out why.

First, I remember that this has to do with the diffraction of sound. So, diffraction is the phenomenon where waves bend around obstacles. In this case, the obstacle is a slit in the speaker enclosure. The problem mentions it's a long rectangular slit, so I think that implies it's a single slit diffraction problem.

I recall that single-slit diffraction can be described by the single-slit diffraction formula, which is:

\[ d \sin \theta = m \lambda \]

where:
- \( d \) is the slit width,
- \( \theta \) is the angle from the normal,
- \( m \) is the diffraction order (a positive integer, starting from 0),
- \( \lambda \) is the wavelength of the sound.

The problem states that the angle is 45 degrees, so \( \theta = 45^\circ \). The slit is 0.14 m across, so \( d = 0.14 \) m. The sound wave is moving at 350 m/s, so the speed of sound \( v \) is 350 m/s. I need to find the frequency \( f \) at which the first minimum occurs, which corresponds to \( m = 1 \) (the first-order diffraction minimum). 

Wait, hold on. Is it the first-order minimum? I think so because the question is about the sound first disappearing, which would be the first destructive interference, the first minimum. So yes, \( m = 1 \).

First, I need to find the wavelength \( \lambda \) of the sound. Since the speed of sound is given by \( v = f \lambda \), rearranging we get:

\[ \lambda = \frac{v}{f} \]

But I don't know \( f \) yet. So, perhaps I can express \( \lambda \) in terms of \( f \) and plug it into the diffraction equation.

From the diffraction formula:

\[ d \sin \theta = m \lambda \]

Plugging \( m = 1 \), \( d = 0.14 \) m, and \( \theta = 45^\circ \):

\[ 0.14 \sin 45^\circ = 1 \times \lambda \]

I can compute \( \sin 45^\circ \) which is \( \frac{\sqrt{2}}{2} \approx 0.7071 \).

So,

\[ 0.14 \times 0.7071 = \lambda \]

Calculating that:

\[ 0.14 \times 0.7071 \approx 0.098999 \approx 0.099 \, \text{m} \]

So, \( \lambda \approx 0.099 \) m.

Now, since \( v = f \lambda \), I can solve for \( f \):

\[ f = \frac{v}{\lambda} \]

Given \( v = 350 \) m/s and \( \lambda \approx 0.099 \) m,

\[ f = \frac{350}{0.099} \approx \frac{350}{0.1} \approx 3500 \, \text{Hz} \]

Okay, so I have this physics problem here about sound waves diffracting out of a speaker enclosure. The question is asking at what frequency the sound will first disappear at a 45-degree angle from the normal to the speaker face. The opening is a long rectangular slit 0.14 meters across. The options given are A. 500 Hz, B. 1,750 Hz, C. 2,750 Hz, and D. 3,500 Hz. And the correct answer is supposed to be B, 1,750 Hz. Hmm, I need to figure out why.

First, I remember that when sound waves pass through a slit, diffraction occurs. This is called single-slit diffraction. The formula for the minima in single-slit diffraction is given by:

\[ d \sin \theta = m \lambda \]

Where:
- \( d \) is the slit width,
- \( \theta \) is the angle from the normal,
- \( m \) is the order of the minimum (m = 1, 2, 3, ...),
- \( \lambda \) is the wavelength of the sound.

The question is asking for the frequency at which the sound first disappears, which corresponds to the first minimum, so m = 1.

I need to find the frequency \( f \), so I should relate the wavelength \( \lambda \) to the frequency. The speed of sound \( v \) is given as 350 m/s. The formula for wavelength is:

\[ \lambda = \frac{v}{f} \]

So, I can substitute this into the diffraction formula:

\[ d \sin \theta = m \left( \frac{v}{f} \right) \]

Let me rearrange this to solve for frequency:

\[ f = \frac{v}{d \sin \theta \times m} \]

Given:
- \( d = 0.14 \) m,
- \( \theta = 45^\circ \),
- \( m = 1 \),
- \( v = 350 \) m/s.

Plugging these into the formula:

\[ f = \frac{350}{0.14 \times \sin(45^\circ) \times 1} \]

I need to calculate \( \sin(45^\circ) \). I remember that \( \sin(45^\circ) = \frac{\sqrt{2}}{2} \approx 0.7071 \).

So substituting that in:

\[ f = \frac{350}{0.14 \times 0.7071} \]

0.14 multiplied by 0.7071. Let's calculate that.

0.14 * 0.7071 ≈ 0.14 * 0.7071 ≈ 0.098999

Okay, so I have this physics problem here about sound diffraction. Hmm, let's read it again. It says that sound waves are moving at 350 m/s and they're diffracting out of a speaker enclosure with a long rectangular slit that's 0.14 meters across. The question is asking at about what frequency the sound will first disappear at an angle of 45 degrees from the normal to the speaker face. The options are A. 500 Hz, B. 1,750 Hz, C. 2,750 Hz, D. 3,500 Hz. The correct answer is supposed to be B. 1,750 Hz. I need to understand why that is.

Alright, so let's break this down. First, I remember that when sound waves come out of a slit, they can diffract around the edges. This is called diffraction. There's a formula for the angle at which the sound first disappears, which is the angle where the path difference equals the wavelength. I think this is called the single-slit diffraction formula.

The formula for the angle θ (theta) where the first minimum occurs is given by:

sinθ = λ / (a)

Where:
- λ is the wavelength of the sound
- a is the slit width

Okay, so I need to find the frequency first because the wavelength is related to the speed of sound. The speed of sound is given as 350 m/s. So, the formula for wavelength λ is:

λ = v / f

Where v is the velocity, so 350 m/s, and f is the frequency we need to find.

So, plugging that into the diffraction formula:

sinθ = (v / f) / a

Which can be rearranged to solve for f:

f = v / (a * sinθ)

Given that θ is 45 degrees, and a is 0.14 meters.

Let me write that out:

f = 350 / (0.14 * sin(45°))

I think sin(45°) is √2/2, which is approximately 0.7071.

So plugging that in:

f = 350 / (0.14 * 0.7071)

This is called diffraction cancellation or destructive interference. The problem is asking for the frequency at which this happens at a 45-degree angle.

\[ \sin(\theta) = \frac{\lambda}{d} \]

- \(\theta\) is the angle from the normal,
- \(\lambda\) is the wavelength of the sound,
- \(d\) is the width of the slit.

Alright, so I've got this problem about sound diffraction from a speaker enclosure. Let me try to work through it step by step. 

The question says: Sound waves moving at 350 m/s diffract out of a speaker enclosure with an opening that's a long rectangular slit 0.14 m across. We need to find the frequency at which the sound first disappears at an angle of 45 degrees from the normal to the speaker face. The options are A. 500 Hz, B. 1,750 Hz, C. 2,750 Hz, D. 3,500 Hz. The correct answer is supposedly B, 1,750 Hz. Hmm, I need to figure out why that is the case.

First, I remember that when a sound wave diffracts around an opening, it undergoes a phenomenon called diffraction. For a slit, the diffraction is given by the Fraunhofer diffraction formula. But wait, actually, in the case of a slit, the diffraction pattern is somewhat different from a circular aperture. For a long, narrow slit (which this is, since it's 0.14 m across), the diffraction pattern is similar to a single slit, with a central bright band and then alternating minima and maxima.

The formula for the minima in the diffraction pattern for a single slit is given by:

d * sin(theta) = m * lambda

Where:
- d is the slit width (0.14 m in this case),
- theta is the angle from the normal,
- m is the order of the minimum (m = 1, 2, 3...),
- lambda is the wavelength of the sound in the medium.

In this problem, the sound is moving at 350 m/s, so I need to find the wavelength. The speed of sound in air is typically 343 m/s at 20°C, but here it's given as 350 m/s. I can still use the same approach.

The speed of sound (v) is related to the wavelength (lambda) and the frequency (f) by the equation:

v = f * lambda

So, lambda = v / f.

But wait, since we don't know the frequency yet, maybe I can rearrange the diffraction formula to solve for frequency.

We need to find the first minimum, which occurs at m = 1. The angle given is 45 degrees. Let me plug these values into the formula.

So, 0.14 m * sin(45°) = 1 * lambda

First, compute sin(45°). That's sqrt(2)/2, which is approximately 0.7071.

So, lambda = 0.14 * 0.7071

Calculating that: 0.14 * 0.7071 ≈ 0.09899 meters, which is about 0.099 meters.

Now, lambda is approximately 0.099 m.

But we know that lambda = v / f, so rearranging for f gives:

f = v / lambda

f = 350 / 0.099

0.099 * 3500 ≈ 346.5

Alright, so I have this problem about sound diffraction from a slit. Let me try to understand what it's asking. It says: "Sound waves moving at 350 m/s diffract out of a speaker enclosure with an opening that is a long rectangular slit 0.14 m across. At about what frequency will the sound first disappear at an angle of 45 degrees from the normal to the speaker face?" The options are A. 500 Hz, B. 1,750 Hz, C. 2,750 Hz, D. 3,500 Hz. The correct answer is supposed to be B. 1,750 Hz. Hmm, okay.

I remember that when sound waves pass through a slit or an aperture, they can diffract, meaning they spread out, kind of like how light bends around obstacles. The angle at which the sound first disappears is called the diffraction angle, right? So, we need to find the frequency where this happens at 45 degrees.

First, let me note down the given information:

- Speed of sound, \( v = 350 \) m/s
- Slit width, \( a = 0.14 \) m
- Diffraction angle, \( \theta = 45^\circ \)

I think the formula for the diffraction angle in this case is similar to the single-slit diffraction formula. For single-slit diffraction, the condition for destructive interference (which causes the sound to disappear) is given by:

\( \sin \theta = \frac{\lambda}{a} \)

Where \( \lambda \) is the wavelength of the sound in air.

So, if I can find \( \lambda \), I can relate it to the frequency \( f \) because \( \lambda = v / f \).

Let me write that down:

\( \sin \theta = \frac{\lambda}{a} \)

So, \( \lambda = a \sin \theta \)

Then, \( f = v / \lambda = v / (a \sin \theta) \)

Alright, so substituting in the values:

\( f = 350 / (0.14 \times \sin 45^\circ) \)

Let me compute \( \sin 45^\circ \). I know that \( \sin 45^\circ = \frac{\sqrt{2}}{2} \approx 0.7071 \).

So, \( f = 350 / (0.14 \times 0.7071) \)

Let me compute the denominator first: \( 0.14 \times 0.7071 \).

0.14 times 0.7 is 0.098, and 0.14 times 0.0071 is approximately 0.000994. So, adding them together gives roughly 0.098994.

So, \( f \approx 350 / 0.098994 \)

That angle is given as 45 degrees from the normal.

--------------------------------------------------
Alright, so I have this physics problem here about sound diffraction. Hmm, let me try to figure it out step by step. The question says that sound waves are moving at 350 m/s and they're diffracting out of a speaker enclosure with a long rectangular slit that's 0.14 m across. The problem is asking at what frequency will the sound first disappear at a 45-degree angle from the normal to the speaker face. The options are A. 500 Hz, B. 1,750 Hz, C. 2,750 Hz, D. 3,500 Hz. And it's stated that the correct answer is B, 1,750 Hz. But let me try to work through it myself to understand why.

First, I remember that when sound waves pass through a slit or an opening, they diffract, creating a diffraction pattern. The pattern includes a central bright spot and then alternating dark and bright fringes. The first dark fringe is where the sound first disappears, which is what the question is referring to.

I think this has to do with the single-slit diffraction formula. The condition for the first dark fringe (the first minima) in single-slit diffraction is given by:

a * sin(theta) = m * lambda

Where:
- a is the slit width,
- theta is the angle from the normal to the slit,
- m is the order of the minima (for the first minima, m = 1),
- lambda is the wavelength of the sound.

The problem gives the angle as 45 degrees, so theta is 45 degrees. The slit width is 0.14 m across, so that's 'a'. The speed of sound is given as 350 m/s, from which we can find the wavelength using the speed formula:

First, I remember that when sound waves diffract around an opening, there's a phenomenon called diffraction. One common type is single-slit diffraction. The formula for the diffraction angle in the single-slit case is given by:

\[

\]

Where:
- \(\theta\) is the diffraction angle,
- \(\lambda\) is the wavelength of the sound,
- \(\delta\) is the size of the slit.

The problem is asking for the frequency at which the sound first disappears at 45 degrees. That means the first diffraction minimum, which is when the path difference causes destructive interference. So, at that angle, the path difference plus the slit width should equal an integer multiple of the wavelength.

But wait, hold on. The formula I mentioned earlier is for the first-order diffraction. However, for the first minimum (the first destructive interference), the condition is:

\[
d \sin \theta = m \lambda
\]

Where:
- \(d\) is the slit width,
- \(m\) is the order of the diffraction,
- \(\lambda\) is the wavelength.

Since the sound first disappears at 45 degrees, that should be the first-order minimum, so \(m = 1\).

Given:
- The speed of sound, \(v = 350 \) m/s,
- Slit width, \(\delta = 0.14 \) m,
- Angle, \(\theta = 45^\circ\).

First, let's find the wavelength \(\lambda\). I know that the speed of sound is related to the wavelength and frequency by:

\[
v = f \lambda
\]

So,

\[
\lambda = \frac{v}{f}
\]

Our goal is to find the frequency \(f\), so we'll substitute \(\lambda\) in the diffraction condition.

From the diffraction condition:

\[
d \sin \theta = m \lambda
\]

Substituting \(\lambda = v/f\):

\[
d \sin \theta = m \frac{v}{f}
\]

We can rearrange this to solve for \(f\):

\[
f = \frac{m v}{d \sin \theta}
\]

Plugging in the known values:

- \(m = 1\),
- \(v = 350 \) m/s,
- \(d = 0.14 \) m,
- \(\sin 45^\circ = \frac{\sqrt{2}}{2} \approx 0.7071\).

Alright, so I have this physics problem about sound diffraction from a slit. The question is asking about the frequency at which sound first disappears at a 45-degree angle from the normal to the speaker face. The speaker has a slit that's 0.14 meters across. The speed of the sound is given as 350 m/s. The options are A. 500 Hz, B. 1,750 Hz, C. 2,750 Hz, D. 3,500 Hz. The correct answer is said to be B, 1,750 Hz, but I want to figure out why.

First, I remember that when a sound wave comes out of a slit, it's called diffraction. There are two types: single-slit and double-slit. Since the question mentions a long rectangular slit, I think it's single-slit diffraction. In single-slit diffraction, the sound waves interfere with each other, and there are minima where the sound doesn't pass through.

The formula for the minima in single-slit diffraction is given by:

\[ d \sin \theta = m \lambda \]

Where:
- \( d \) is the slit width,
- \( \theta \) is the angle from the normal,
- \( m \) is the order of the minimum (m = 1, 2, 3...),
- \( \lambda \) is the wavelength of the sound.

We need to find the frequency \( f \) that corresponds to the first minimum, which is when \( m = 1 \), at \( \theta = 45^\circ \).

So, the wavelength \( \lambda \) can be calculated using the speed of sound and the frequency:

\[ \lambda = v / f \]

Where \( v \) is the speed of sound, which is 350 m/s.

So, plugging into the diffraction formula:

\[ d \sin \theta = m \lambda \]
\[ d \sin \theta = m (v / f) \]

We need to solve for \( f \):

\[ f = v / (d \sin \theta \cdot m) \]

Given:
- \( d = 0.14 \) m,
- \( \theta = 45^\circ \),
- \( m = 1 \),
- \( v = 350 \) m/s.

So plugging in the numbers:

\[ f = 350 / (0.14 \times \sin(45^\circ) \times 1) \]

First, calculate \( \sin(45^\circ) \). I remember that \( \sin(45^\circ) = \sqrt{2}/2 \approx 0.7071 \).

So,

\[ f = 350 / (0.14 \times 0.7071) \]

0.14 * 0.7071 ≈ 0.14 * 0.7071 ≈ 0.099 m.

$$

$$

Where:
- \(\theta\) is the diffraction angle,
- \(\lambda\) is the wavelength of the sound,

\[
